		"content": {
			"rendered": "<h3>Cloud-based Platform for Wi-Fi Device Management</h3>\n<p>Principal Interaction Designer in charge of UX for the company&#8217;s 6 interactive products:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Personal home/business wi-fi manager (iOS + Android) (now <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.cloudmondo.consumer\">blazeX</a>)</li>\n<li>Tablet-based Network Operation Center for cloud-managed wi-fi devices (iOS + Android) (now <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.cloudmondo.pocketNOQ\">blazeNOQ</a>)</li>\n<li>Web-based Network Operation Center for cloud-managed wi-fi devices (Web)</li>\n<li>Cloud-managed wi-fi device provisioning app  (Android)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>I was in charge of:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Understanding requirements from customers and stakeholders</li>\n<li>Translating business requirements and platform constrains into user-oriented and user-friendly interfaces</li>\n<li>Understanding the intricacies of the platform (easy set-up of cloud-based agent-managed &#8216;routers&#8217; by both technicians and end-users)</li>\n<li>Defining the workflows, screens, processes and interactions for the user interface</li>\n<li>Coordinating with the development team to get designs into production pipeline</li>\n<li>User-oriented and functionality QA control</li>\n<li>Management of the app&#8217;s online access points (Google Play Store / Apple App Store)</li>\n</ul>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-1 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-1 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: both;' />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Understanding and strategy</strong></p>\n<p>The first couple of weeks one visual designer and I interviewed all internal stakeholders and most of the developers to get a wide understanding of who we were targeting and what were we building.</p>\n<p>Then we made a workshop with all the stakeholders and engineers to discover the user flow hypotheses and create profiles of the personae hypotheses we wanted to test on the product. We also created hypotheses for the customer journeys we&#8217;d create in order to understand where to maximise value and where our platform will offer possible pain points.</p>\n<p>We also sat down with developers to understand in detail how the micro-services worked so we could have a good idea on how the experience worked on the backend and how that would affect the user experience. We created detailed flows of each process.</p></blockquote>\n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"2426\" />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Designing the user flows</strong></p>\n<p>Next, I took a shot at the wireframes of the app, by first defining the user needs and goals and then defining a flow for each goal. I documented all the process on Confluence so developers had quick access to flows and screens and for the whole process to be easily updatable so we could move faster to the flows we would want to build.</p></blockquote>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-3 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-3 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: Within a cadence of two-week sprints, we aim to have interface releases in every sprint, and immediately afterwards we tested them with real-life scenarios, and when possible, with real-life prospect customers.</p>\n<p>We managed to deliver all 6 apps within the 6-month deadline for a pilot programme abroad.</p></blockquote>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n",

			"rendered": "<h3>Online platform for an <em>Internet of Things</em> employment and education service</h3>\n<p>Cisco Corporate Social Responsibility wanted to create an online platform to support their initiative to educate the next generation of <em>Internet of Things</em> Specialists together with their strategic partners. I designed an online education platform to be tested in a pilot run for the program. What I did was:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Interviewed</strong> key stakeholders</li>\n<li>Created a <strong>strategic vision</strong> for the program&#8217;s platform</li>\n<li>Helped <strong>define key events</strong> on the desired customer experience for the program</li>\n<li>Presented <strong>ideas as a prototype</strong> that presented a user journey in an interactive way</li>\n<li><strong>Tested</strong> the prototype with internal resources, subject-matter experts and stakeholders</li>\n<li>Refined the solution by <strong>iterating on the prototype</strong> and presenting to key stakeholders</li>\n<li><strong>Lead a team</strong> of interaction and visual designers in the creation of an MVP platform for a test pilot program</li>\n<li>Kept an open conversation at all times with all key stakeholders to <strong>address and integrate their needs and feedback</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Coded a fully-functioning prototype</strong> (html5/bootstrap/javascript/json db) as design reference and specification for the development team</li>\n<li><strong>Interfaced with the development team</strong> to make sure functionality aligned with resources, platform capabilities and completion timeframe</li>\n</ul>\n<p>I also helped CSR create a future vision of the program as an interactive prototype, allowing stakeholders to understand the ideas and the functionality of the proposed solution by experiencing it first hand.</p>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-5 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Sketches</strong></p>\n<p>I was tasked with the creation of an online platform to support a comprehensive education-to-employment pilot program that addresses IT workforce skill gaps and prepares students for emerging IT careers in the digital economy, and empowers them to harness a $19 trillion global opportunity.</p>\n<p>I started by meeting key stakeholders around the company (educators, technicians, project managers, directors, former students of the Cisco Networking Academy), and by sketching a simple idea of an education program platform would be like.</p></blockquote>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-6 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-6 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Design sprint deliverables</strong></p>\n<p>We then brought in a design agency named Idean to help us define the style and visual language of the online platform.</p>\n<p>I lead a series of 6 weekly design sprints that covered the larger areas of the online platform: Forums, Dashboard, Student Profile, Lesson Pages, Project Pages and Student Assessment.</p>\n<p>A team of one Interaction Designer and two Visual Designers lead by me started working every week on the wires for one of the sections and, staggered, the visuals for the section completed the previous week.</p>\n<p>We hold stand-ups every other day and a weekly sync with all Project Managers and key stakeholders, where we would get their feedback and suggestions and align with specific needs from parallel projects: job board, sudent assessments, learning management system and education platform.</p></blockquote>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-10 />\n\t</div>\n\n<blockquote><p><strong>Cisco SkillZone – Final Prototype (HTML/CSS/JS/Bootstrap)</strong></p>\n<p>Every week we’ll have at hand the deliverables for a specific section that would be immediately embedded into a fully functional prototype (html/css/javascript jquery/bootstrap) that I built myself from scratch.</p>\n<p>I then started having tri-weekly meetings with the development team that started building the interface. Since they had access to the final fully-functional prototype they already had a precise idea of what they were building. In our meetings we went together through the site and solved together any minor or major issue they might run into.</p>\n<p>Thanks to the team work and the collaboration level, we were able to build the whole site in less than 5 months with a team of just only 3-4 developers.</p>\n<p>I also took advantage of the working prototype to present to other stakeholders and managers, and to conduct further testing on subject matter experts and other individuals similar to the target audience.</p></blockquote>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p><!--[gallery ids=\"1297,1298,1289,1288,1304,1305,1302,1303,1301,1300,1290,1291,1293\"]\n\n--></p>\n",

			"rendered": "<p>Design of on-boarding experience for a tablet-integrated self-servicing platform for small business.</p>\n<p>The main objective of my proposal was to have a minimally simple login 1-2-3 process (top row on diagrams) while offering users more detailed information like apps downloaded and technical steps taken when they tapped on the numbers (lower rows).</p>\n<blockquote><p>I helped create a process that simplifies the experience to the bare minimum necessary: the space where to see apps downloading and being able to explore them right away, as playing with your new apps is the best use of the on-boarding&#8217;s waiting time.</p></blockquote>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-11 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-11 .gallery-item 		"content": {
			"rendered": "<h3>Intel.com Responsive Web Platform Redesign</h3>\n<p>Redesign of the whole Intel.com property, intended to improve the user experience of both visitors and content providers, including:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Making the whole platform responsive, simplifying presentation and maintenance for all touchpoints.</li>\n<li>Improving the user experience by creating <em>Storytelling</em> boilerplates for content owners to start from, thus improving the likes of better content presentation.</li>\n<li>Eliminating pain points for Intel content providers by simplifying the content management platform from 47 modules to 9 to choose from when adding content.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Most of the wireframes presented here were only a visual reference from where to start the real design process, which happened in real code. We made all design decisions directly on an online prototype. We also used this prototype to present to the client, who tested it on 27 different devices in their test lab, ranging from iPhones to touchscreen-enabled ultrabooks, to ultrawide-screen monitors.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-13 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-13 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top: 			"rendered": "<p>Creation of a mobile support app for the Ericsson global mobile salesforce, including tools that will support their work across the globe.</p>\n<p>I helped define a flexible and robust platform with a simple, easily-understandable interface that integrated more than 10 existing platforms and services. The design accomplished the following goals:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Create a central tool with a simple interface, easy to use at home and while traveling anywhere in the world</li>\n<li>Robustly scale by easily adding functionality and other growing services</li>\n<li>Integrate different tools and sites with different technologies and platforms in a simple, add-on, manner</li>\n<li>Be easy to 	{
		"id": 812,
		"date": "2013-03-11T01:51:30",
		"date_gmt": "2013-03-11T01:51:30",
		"guid": {
			"rendered": "http://www.frwrd.net/?p=812"
		},
		"modified": "2017-07-24T15:00:51",
		"modified_gmt": "2017-07-24T15:00:51",
		"slug": "patch-2-0",
		"status": "publish",
		"type": "jetpack-portfolio",
		"link": "https://victorzambrano.com/portfolio/patch-2-0/",
		"title": {
			"rendered": "Patch.com 2.0"
		},
		"content": {
			"rendered": "<h3>Brief</h3>\n<p>Redesign of the Patch platform, focussed on a community approach.</p>\n<p>We made Patch from an online newspaper to an online community hub. We gave the community a platform where to exchange and communicate with each other, thus empowering them and enhancing the town&#8217;s interconnections, communication and social tissue.</p>\n<h3>Process</h3>\n<p>After a nationwide ethnographical user research we designed an <strong>Alpha Version</strong> as a platform of multi-use online groups. Patch users could create their own groups, follow other people&#8217;s groups and invite people from town to those groups. It was launched as an &#8220;Alpha&#8221; release in five towns around Long Island, NY. It was closely followed by user-centred testing and iterative design updates.</p>\n<p>Taking into account the learnings from the recently deployed Alpha Version, a <strong>Release Version</strong> was designed. After several iterations and paired usability testing rounds we presented a simplified system made of editorial-driven news and publicly-open community boards. This way we helped Patch users understand and interact with their town community. It was deployed in all of 900+ Patch towns across the US.</p>\n<p>I was integral part of:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>User research and constant rounds of usability testing</li>\n<li>The strategy by understanding and communicating the impact of the new features on product adoption and impact</li>\n<li>The vision and functionality of the product</li>\n<li>Leading the UX iterate the product into an Alpha Version design</li>\n<li>Understanding the results and learnings from the Alpha Version</li>\n<li>Leading the UX to design a Final product incorporating the learnings from the Alpha Version metrics, functionality and usability testings</li>\n</ul>\n<h3>Results</h3>\n<p>We made a phenomenal work. In some towns the UGC engagement went up to 6% (sites like Huffington Post get around 1%), and it grew even in towns previously with small engagement.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n\t\t<style 			"rendered": "Grid OS Interface"

		"content": {
			"rendered": "<h2>The role</h2>\n<p>I lead the UX and UI Direction for the final production of the GridOS for the Grid10 tablet and the Grid4 smartphone. My responsibilities included the overall interaction, information architecture and design direction for the final design process of the Grid Operative System (GridOS) and all native applications (messages, video, photos, video chat, address book, contextual menus, and filesystem) for the android-based <a title=\"Grid 10 Tablet\" href=\"http://www.engadget.com/2011/10/05/grid10-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Grid10 Tablet</a> and the  <a title=\"Grid 4 Touch Smartphone\" href=\"http://www.engadget.com/2011/08/16/hands-on-with-fusion-garages-grid-10-tablet-and-grid-4-smartpho/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Grid4 Smartphone</a>, managing a team of 7 graphic, motion-graphic and interaction designers.</p>\n<h2>The results</h2>\n<p>I helped transform a vision of an interface to be integrated on top of the Android OS into a robust, simple and usable interface. With a team of 5 Motion Graphic Designers and 2 Visual Designers I redesigned several of the existing applications (Photos, Videos, Messages, Calendar, Global Search, Notifications Centre and Contextual Menu) and designed others from scratch (&#8220;Chrome-less&#8221; Browser, Maps, Keyboard, Volume, Cross-device App AutoSync) working in extremely tight deadlines and an offshore development team based in Singapore and other countries in Southeast Asia.</p>\n<h2>The process</h2>\n<p>All deliveries were made in PSD files and very precise AfterEffects videos that described the interactions in great detail so development will perfectly align with the vision. We defined a workflow with no wireframes to interpret and understand, but instead we delivered videos that would tell a perfect story of the exact experience of the interaction with which users would be presented and delighted. We delivered in a tight cycle, getting specific business requirements every morning and delivering defined assets and guidance in a 24-to-48 hour iteration rounds.</p>\n<h2>The reviews</h2>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;The Grid software is clever and innovative in many ways&#8221;<br />\n&#8212; <a href=\"http://allthingsd.com/20111005/grid-10-tablet-hides-android-under-its-own-radical-design/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Walter Mossberg reviews the Grid 10 Tablet</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><a id=\"5b1f51cae694c\" rel=\"wp-video-lightbox\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MZNaT8eq2CI&width=640&height=480\" title=\"\"><div class=\"wpvl_auto_thumb_box_wrapper\"><div class=\"wpvl_auto_thumb_box\"><img src=\"https://img.youtube.com/vi/MZNaT8eq2CI/0.jpg\" class=\"video_lightbox_auto_anchor_image\" alt=\"\" /><div class=\"wpvl_auto_thumb_play\"><img src=\"https://victorzambrano.com/wp-content/plugins/wp-video-lightbox/images/play.png\" class=\"wpvl_playbutton\" /></div></div></div></a>    <script>\r\n    /* 		"title": {
			"rendered": "BMW EV Dashboard"
		},
		"content": {
			"rendered": "<p>Strategy, Design Concepts and User Experience Architecture for the BMW Electric Vehicle Dashboard interactive/mobile application on the BMW Activate The Future website.</p>\n<p><strong>The need:</strong> After we helped BMW successfully launch an iOS/Android app to help people understand if an electric vehicle was for them, they came back to us asking to make an online application to tell visitors the history of energy.</p>\n<p><strong>The process:</strong> After scrupulous analysis and taking into account the timeline for the launch of the BMW EV iOS/Android app, my team and I suggested BMW America to take advantage of the recently released iOS/Android app and create a web app for those interested in getting more information about their compatibility with an electric vehicle, whereas users of the app or not.</p>\n<p><strong>The solution:</strong> The BMW Electric Vehicle Dashboard shows you the impact of electric vehicles on the environment (minimal) and your wallet (maximal). The iPhone/Android app allows users to log their commutes by syncing trips to the online dashboard. Connecting the BMW EV app to the <em>EV Dashboard</em> on BMWActivatethefuture.com, or using it as a standalone web app, visitors would be able to see what impact driving an EV would have for their life and the world, comparing their data to national averages. Different behaviors earn you different badges, as you learn more about how you drive and what the impact of an EV would be.</p>\n<p><strong>The result:</strong> An astoundingly successful campaign that won awards and never stop delighting, and informing, audiences.</p>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class='youtube-player' type='text/html' width='640' height='390' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/FxLWEagftsA?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;start=51&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></span></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-20 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-20 .gallery-item 			"rendered": "Generation Green (British Gas)"
		},
		"content": {
			"rendered": "<p>Generation Green is a schools and community programme from British Gas, devised to promote environmental awareness by giving schools and parents advice and easy to take actions which can earn them green leaves for their school.</p>\n<p>The generation green site was conceived under a simple principle: teachers don&#8217;t have much free time, and any supporting service to be offered to them had to be simple yet with enough substance for the schools to consider introducing it into their already busy study programmes.</p>\n<p>Most of the site&#8217;s interactive process are either triggered by simple calls to action, or managed as linear processes that won&#8217;t take more than 5 minutes to complete.</p>\n<p>In order to facilitate the transition and learning from the viewing to the managing of the site, the administrating section is just a series of active buttons on top of the same page view, and all interactive tasks occur inline, in simple 3- to 4-step linear processes.</p>\n<p>The whole wireframing process was conducted in the Axure RP application, thus allowing a working prototype in every step of the wireframing process, greatly simplifying the client&#8217;s understanding of the site, and allowing us to directly test the iterations on professors and other knowledgeable stockholders. This allowed our team to take a rather small project and convert it into a comprehensive, robust, full-fledged nationwide programme, with the client&#8217;s idea of what the final product will be like all along the process path.</p>\n\n\t\t<style type='text/css'>\n\t\t\t#gallery-21 {\n\t\t\t\tmargin: auto;\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t#gallery-21 .gallery-item {\n\t\t\t\tfloat: left;\n\t\t\t\tmargin-top:
